arXiv:2305.03229v2  [math.AP]  15 May 2023TOLLMIEN-SCHLICHTING WAVES IN THE SUBSONIC REGIME
NADER MASMOUDI, YUXI WANG, DI WU, AND ZHIFEI ZHANG
Abstract. The Tollmien-Schlichting (T-S) waves play a key role in the e arly stages of
boundary layer transition. In a breakthrough work [13], Gre nier, Guo and Nguyen gave
the ﬁrst rigorous construction of the T-S waves of temporal m ode for the incompressible
ﬂuid. Yang and Zhang [27] recently made an important contrib ution by constructing the
compressible T-S waves of temporal mode for certain boundar y layer proﬁles with Mach
number m <1√
3. In this paper, we construct the T-S waves of both temporal mo de and
spatial mode to the linearized compressible Navier-Stokes system around the boundary layer
ﬂow in the whole subsonic regime m <1, including the Blasius proﬁle. Our approach is
based on a novel iteration scheme between the quasi-incompr essible and quasi-compressible
systems, with a key ingredient being the solution of an Orr-S ommerfeld type equation using
a new Airy-Airy-Rayleighiteration instead of Rayleigh-Ai ry iteration introduced by Grenier,
Guo and Nguyen. We believe the method developed in this work c an be applied in solving
other related problems for subsonic ﬂows.
1.Introduction
In this paper, we are concerned with the stability problem fo r an isentropic compressible
ﬂow over a ﬂat plate at high Reynolds number regime Re≫1. The motion of the ﬂuid is
described by the non-dimensional compressible Navier-Sto kes system

∂tρν+∇·(ρνUν) = 0,
ρν/parenleftbig
∂tUν+Uν·∇Uν/parenrightbig
−µν∆Uν−λν∇∇·Uν+∇P(ρν) = 0,
Uν|y=0= 0.(1.1)
Hereρνis the density, Uνis the velocity, and P(ρν) is the pressure. Here µ,λare the viscosity
coeﬃcients and ν >0 is propositional to Re−1.
At high Reynolds number, the behavior of the ﬂow away from the boundary can be de-
scribed by the Euler equations and the behavior near the boun dary can be described by the
Prandtl equation. For the outer ﬂow ρe= 1,Ue= (1,0), the behavior of the solution could
be described by the Blasius solution, which is a self-simila r solution of the steady Prandtl
equation and takes the form
(uB,vB) =/parenleftBig
f′(ζ),1

1
2ff′′+f′′′= 0, f(0) =f′(0) = 0,lim
ζ→+∞f′(ζ) = 1.
The Blasius solution has been experimentally conﬁrmed with remarkable accuracy as a basic
ﬂow over a ﬂat plate [25] . In a remarkable work [21], Iyer and M asmoudi justify the Prandtl
expansion with the Blasius solution as a leading order appro ximation of the steady incom-
pressible Navier-Stokes equations. In a recent work [18], G uo, Wang and Zhang prove that
the Blasius solution is also a stable solution of the unstead y Prandtl equation. This gives

another indication why the Blasius solution is reasonable a s a basic ﬂow. See [17, 19, 20, 26]
and references therein for more related works.

For convenience, we deﬁne the linear operator in (1.3) by L.
In this paper, we will seek two kinds of important unstable mo des, which are so called
Tollmien-Schlichting (T-S) waves.
(1)Temporal mode :α∈Randc∈C. Whenα >0 and Imc=ci>0, this kind of
solution will grow in time;
(2)Spatial mode :α∈Candαc∈R. When Im α=αi<0, this kind of solution
will grow along the streamwise direction x. So, it is more relevant in physics and the
growth rate −αiis a key quantity of eNcriterion in the boundary layer transition.
For the incompressible ﬂuid, the construction of T-S waves s tarted with a series of clas-
sical works by Heisenberg, Tollmien, Schlichting, C. C. Lin etc. [23, 7]. Based on the
asymptotic analysis, they found that there exist lower and u pper marginal stability branches
αlow(ν),αup(ν) depending on the proﬁle Us(y) so that when α∈(αlow,αup), the Orr-
Sommerfeld equation exist unstable solutions with Im( c)>0. In a breakthrough work
[13], Grenier, Guo and Nyugen constructed the T-S waves of te mporal mode for αlying in
an interval [a,b] with αlow≪a < b≪αupfor generic ﬂows Us(y). Moreover, they de-
velop a robust Rayleigh-Airy iteration method to solve the O rr-Sommerfeld equation. Let
us refer to [10, 11, 9, 8, 5, 6, 15, 16] and references therein f or more works on nonlinearTOLLMIEN-SCHLICHTING WAVES IN THE SUBSONIC REGIME 3
stability(instability) of boundary layer ﬂows. Let us refe r to [24, 14, 1, 3, 4] for the linear
stability results about the channel ﬂow or pipe ﬂow.
In a recent important work [27], Yang and Zhang give a ﬁrst rig orous construction of
the compressible T-S waves of temporal mode for αnear the lower branch αlowwhen the
Mach number m <1√
3for a class of boundary layer proﬁles satisfying strong stru cture
assumptions, which excludes the Blasius proﬁle. Their proo f does not use the Rayleigh-Airy
iteration method developed in [13]. Instead, they develope d a quai-compressible and Stokes
iteration.
Throughout this paper, we make the following structure assu mptions on the proﬁle Us(Y):

Let us give some remarks on our results.
(1) This is the ﬁrst time that a mixed type unstable mode has be en constructed, which
will grow in both space and time:
|(̺,U1,U2)(t,x,y)| ∼eCν−1

(2) The Blasius proﬁle satisﬁes the structure assumptions ( 1.5).
(3) All the estimates in our paper are uniformly in m∈(0,1). Whenm→0, we can
construct the T-S waves of both temporal mode and spatial mod e for the incompress-
ible ﬂow, where temporal mode was analyzed in [13] by Grenier -Guo-Nguyen. The
vanishing Mach number limit for temporal mode was also obtai ned in the work of
Yang and Zhang [27].
(4) Our method could be used to construct the T-S waves for α∈[a,b] withαlow≪a<
b≪αupas in [13].
(5) For the supersonic ﬂow m>1, there exist inviscid unstable modes, which plays more
dominant role in the boundary layer transition [22]. This wi ll be conducted in future
works.
2.Sketch of the proof

this end, we will introduce a new iteration scheme between th e quasi-incompressible system
(2.1) and the quasi-compressible system(2.4) and start thi s iteration scheme with the slow or
fast solution to the quasi-incompressible system (2.1). Se e the beginning of section 8 for the
detailed description of iteration scheme.

Most of the paper will be devoted to solving the Orr-Sommerfe ld type system:

In the incompressible case, Grenier, Guo and Nguyen [13] int roduce a robust Rayleigh-Airy
iteration scheme to solve the Orr-Sommerfeld equation. How ever, this iteration scheme does
not work in the compressible case due to the fact that the comm utator [Λ,∂2
Y] will lead to
one loss of the derivative. Note that [Λ ,∂2
Y] = 0 when m= 0. To overcome this diﬃculty, we
introduce a new Airy-Airy-Rayleigh iteration scheme. See t he beginning of section 5 for the6 N. MASMOUDI, Y. WANG, D. WU, AND Z. ZHANG
details. To carry out this iteration scheme, we solve the Ray leigh type equation conducted
in section 3:
(Us−c)Λϕ−∂Y(A−1∂YUs)ϕ=F.
The proof is based on an iteration argument in a well-chosen f unctional space. In section 4,
we solve the Airy type equation
ε(∂2

To solve the Airy type equation, we introduce a modiﬁed Lange r transform, which is the
key to avoid using the analyticity of Us(Y). One of key ingredients is the estimate of the
Green function related to the approximate Airy equation, se e Lemma 4.4. Our approach
is diﬀerent from Yang and Zhang [27]. They made strong assumpt ions about the structure
of boundary layer proﬁles, excluding the Blasius ﬂow, to obt ain energy estimates for the
Airy-type equation (2.5) with Mach number m <1/√
3. In contrast, our method provides
pointwise estimates for φin the entire subsonic regime, and includes the Blasius ﬂow b y
relaxing assumptions on the boundary layer proﬁles.

and the system (2.4).
To match the non-slip boundary condition, we will ﬁnd the sol ution (ρ,u,v) of the system
(1.3) with the form
(ρ,u,v) =Cs(ρs,us,vs)+Cf(ρf,uf,vf),

us(0)

By our construction, we have an explicit asymptotic expansi on for the main parts of the slow
mode and fast mode. In a suitable regime of ( α,c), we can ﬁnd a solution of the dispersion
relation via an implicit function theorem. See section 9 for the details.

5.The Orr-Sommerfeld equation
To solve thequasi-incompressible system (2.1), we solve th e following Orr-Sommerfeld(OS)
type equation with general source term F:
εΛ(∂2
Y−α2)φ−(Us−c)Λφ+∂Y(A−1∂YUs)φ=F. (5.1)
We introduce the operators
OS[·] =εΛ(∂2
Y−α2)−(Us−c)Λ+∂Y(A−1∂YUs),
Ray[·] =(Us−c)Λ−∂Y(A−1∂YUs),
Airy[·] =ε(∂2
Y−α2)−(Us−c).
WedevelopanAiry-Airy-Rayleigh iterationtoconstructet hesolutiontotheOrr-Sommerfeld
equation (5.1). More precisely, we start our iteration with
φ(1)=ψ(1,0)+ψ(1,1)+ϕ(1),
whereψ1,0,ψ(1,1)andϕ(1)solve the following equations respectively,
Airy[Λψ(1,0)] =F,
Airy[Λψ(1,1)] =−ε[Λ,∂2
Y]ψ(1,0)−∂Y(A−1∂YUs)ψ(1,0),
Ray[ϕ(1)] =ε[Λ,∂2
Y]ψ(1,1)+∂Y(A−1∂YUs)ψ(1,1).
Then we obtain
OS[φ(1)] =OS[ψ(1,0)]+OS[ψ(1,1)]+OS[ϕ(1)] =εΛ(∂2
Y−α2)ϕ(1)+F.
Now we deﬁne the iteration scheme inductively. For any j≥1,
φ(j+1)=ψ(j+1,0)+ψ(j+1,1)+ϕ(j+1),
whereψ(j+1,0),ψ(j+1,1)andϕ(j+1)solve
Airy[Λψ(j+1,0)] =−εΛ(∂2
Y−α2)ϕ(j),
Airy[Λψ(j+1,1)] =−ε[Λ,∂2
Y]ψ(j+1,0)−∂Y(A−1∂YUs)ψ(j+1,0)
Ray[ϕ(j+1)] =ε[Λ,∂2
Y]ψ(j+1,1)+∂Y(A−1∂YUs)ψ(j+1,1).TOLLMIEN-SCHLICHTING WAVES IN THE SUBSONIC REGIME 45
